mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 200%; color: #000000;">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">}</span></p></td><td style="width: 315.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; color: #000000;">Bangladesh Rubber Industries, a registered Partnership Firm, represented by its Managing Partner, Mr. Ifteker Hussain of 278, Tejgaon Industrial Area, Dhaka and another</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">...Petitioners</span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Versus</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Dine Ara Begum and others<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">...Respondents</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Registration Act (XVI of 1908)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Section 17</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="color: #000000;">A deed of di</span>ssolution of partnership is not required to be registered under section 17 of the Registration Act because the share of a partner in a partnership is essentially moveable property notwithstanding that a part of the partnership property may be immovable. . . . (16)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Pershad Ram Pershad Vs. Sham Sunder and others, AIR 1947 Lahore, 13; Addanki Narayanappa Vs. Bhaskara Krishnappa, AIR 1966 SC 1300; Lui Ying Ping Vs. Leon Fang AI. (1984) 36 DLR (AD) 273; N. Khandervali Saheb (dead) by LRS and another Vs. N. Gudu Sahib (dead) and others (2003) 3 SCC 229;</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">S.V. Chandra Pandian Vs. S. V. Sivalinga Nadar (1993) 1 SCC 589;</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Commissioner of Income Tax, West Bengal, Calcutta Vs. Juggilal Kamalapat, AIR 1967 (SC) 401 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">For the Petitioners:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Mr. Farid Ahmed,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Md. Taufique Hossain, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For Respondent No. 1:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Mr. Mohsin Rashid, Advocate (Mrs. Nazneen Nahar, Advocate with him), instructed by Mr. Syed Mahbubur Rahman, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">Respondent Nos.2-13:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.1pt;"> Not represented.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-variant: small-caps;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, C. J:</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This petition for review arises out of the judgment and order dated 24.05.2016 passed by this Division in Civil Appeal No.01 of 2010 allowing the appeal and setting aside the judgment and order dated 07.08.2008 passed by the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.9268 of 2007 making the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts, leading to the filing of this review petition, in nutshell, are:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Review-petitioner No.1 brought the writ petition on the averment, <em>inter alia</em>, that three full brothers, namely, Noor Hossain, Mosharraf Hossain and Tozammal Hossain and one Saghir Ahmed initially formed a partnership firm under the name and style of Messers East Pakistan Rubber Industries in terms of an agreement of a partnership dated 07.05.1957(that another brother Iqbal Hussain was admitted to the said partnership as a minor). The Government of erstwhile East Pakistan allotted a piece of land measuring 1 (one) acre appertaining to an industrial Plot No.278 at Tejgaon Industrial Area, Dhaka in t<span style="color: #000000;">he name of the said partnership firm on 26.08.1960. The partner, Noor Hussain died on 23.07.1968 leaving behind his two sons, namely, Anwar Husain and Iftekhar Husain, four daughters, Jinnat Husain (Zinat Husain), Jesmin Husain (minor), Israt Husain (minor), Sharmin Husain (</span>minor), a widow Rowshan Ara Hussain and mother Zohra Khatun. They became partners of the said firm as Noor Hossain’s legal heirs. Meanwhile, minor Iqbal Husain having attained majority became a fullfledged partner along with others under a reconstituted deed of partnership dated 24.07.1968. A standard lease deed for a period of 99 years in respect of the said industrial plot was executed on 20.01.1970 and registered on 17.02.1971 between the Government of erstwhile East Pakistan and the said partnership firm. On 31.08.1970, another partner Mosharaf Husain resigned from the partnership business in term of a compromise decree passed in Title Suit No.65 of 1970 in the Third Court of the then learned Subordinate Judge, Dhaka. After liberation war, the name of the firm was changed as Bangladesh Rubber Industries by a deed of rectification. In consequence thereof the change was recorded with the Registrar of Firms. Thereafter, a deed of agreement for dissolution of the firm was executed on 31.12.1975 by the remaining partners, namely, Mrs. Rawshan Ara Hossain, Mr. Iftekhar Hussain, Mr. Anwar Hossain and Miss Zeenat Hossain (heirs of late Noor Hossain) on the one hand and Mr. Tofazammel Hossain, Mr. Iqbal Hossain, Mrs. Zohra Khatun and Mr. Sagir Ahmed, on the other hand, vide Annexure-D under the terms and conditions stated therein. After dissolution of the aforesaid partnership, late Noor Hossain’s heirs, namely, Anwar Hussain and Iftekhar Husain, four daughters, Zinat Hussain, Jesmin Hussain (minor), Ishrat Hussain (minor) and Sharmin Hussain (minor) and widow Rowshan Ara Hussain, executed a fresh partnership deed dated 01.01.1976 (admitting the minors to the benefit of partnership) to run and continue a partnership business vide Annexure-E and they got it registered with the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms under the Partnership Act being Registration No.P.F./22285 (wrongly written P.R.33385) dated 09.11.1976. Thereafter, the heirs of late Tozammel Hussain (i.e. the present respondents) filed an application in the office of writ-respondent No.1 for getting their names mutated in place of Bangladesh Rubber Industries as per their share (i.e. two bighas of land in term of the deed of dissolution, vide Annexure-D). The Senior Assistant Secretary (respondent No.3 in writ petition) on the basis of the aforesaid application served notices upon the parties concerned on 06.02.2005 and 20.02.2007 to appear before the Joint Secretary (respondent No.2 in writ petition) with their respective documents. On hearing both the sides, he rejected the prayer for mutation, vide his letter dated 12.06.2007 (Annexure-I) expressing that the Ministry had no scope to interfere with the matter of mutation since a civil suit was pending in this regard, but nevertheless directed the parties concerned to inform the Government of the fate of the pending suit or the result of the compromise, if made, in the meantime. The further case of the writ petitioner is that after issuance of letter dated 12.06.2007, the present respondent Nos.1 to 3 (respondent Nos.7-9 in writ petition) did not follow the directive of the said notice and beyond the knowledge of present review-petitioner No.1 (petitioner in writ petition) and in collusion with the officials of the Government got the impugned order dated 13.09.2007 (Annexure-J) allowing mutation of their names in respect of two bighas of land without serving any notice whatsoever to them and simultaneously communicated the said order to the Assistant commissioner Land, Tejgaon Circle, Dhaka and other concerned officials for compliance.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the letter dated 13.09.2007 issued by writ-respondent No.1, the writ-petitioners filed a writ petition before the High Court Division and obtained Rule Nisi in Writ Petition No.9268 of 2007.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Writ-respondent Nos.7-9 contested Rule by filing affidavit-in-opposition controverting the material statements made in the writ petition. Their case, in short, is that they accepted the material facts as reproduced in paragraph-2 about the formation of partnership firm on 7th May,1957 under the name of East Pakistan Rubber Industries, subsequent reconstitution of the said firm and ultimate dissolution on 31<sup>st</sup> December 1975 under the terms of the deed of dissolution (vide Annexure-D). The said deed of dissolution narrates (in recitation portion) about the formation of the partnership firm on 14.05.1957 and its subsequent reconstitutions and ultimate dissolution of the said partnership firm on 1st December 1975 on apportions of the shares among the existing partners in the form of land, cash money and good-will of the said firm.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Judges of the High Court Division, upon hearing the parties, by the judgment and order dated 07.08.2008 made the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with judgment and order passed by the High Court Division, the writ-respondents as the leave-petitioners moved this Division by filing Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal Nos.2237 of 2008, on which, leave was granted on 06.01.2009, resulting in Civil Appeal No.01 of 2010. This Division upon hearing the appeal by the judgment and order dated 24.05.2016 allowed the appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the judgment and order dated 24.05.2016 passed by this Division, the writ-petitioner-respondents as the review petitioners filed Review Petition No.315 of 2017 before this Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Farid Ahmed, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the petitioners, submits that Bangladesh Rubber Industries is a registered partnership firm constituted under the provision of Partnership Act,1932 and as such, it is capable of holding immovable property in its own name and to have the title vested in it. Accordingly, the immovable property measuring one acre of land, comprised Industrial Plot No.278 of Tejgaon Industrial Area, Dhaka, having been allotted and transferred by way of perpetual lease deed, it becomes the owner and possessor of the said immovable property, holding the title of the said land and as such, to divest the title of the said immovable property from the partnership firm, a registered deed of transfer is required. Since admittedly, no such deed of transfer was executed and registered by the partnership firm relinquishing its title in the said property in favour of the individual partners, the mutation of names in respect of the said property in the individual names of the partners are palpably illegal and as such, the judgment passed by this Division may be reviewed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mr. Mohosin Rashid, learned Advocate (Mrs. Nazneen Nahar, Advocate with him), appearing on behalf of respondent No.1, on the other hand, supports the judgment delivered by the High Court Division.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have considered the submissions of the learned Senior Advocate for the petitioners and the learned Advocate for respondent No.1, perused the impugned judgment and the materials on record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is admitted that as the disputed property belongs exclusively to the firm, no partner can claim any part of the property as his own and what a partner is entitled to his share of profits only, so long the partnership continues. Upon dissolution of the partnership, his share is his proportion of money representing the firm’s asset including immovable property after liquidation of the partnership debts and liabilities.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">On dissolution of firm each of the partners is entitled to receive his share of assets of the firm to which he was entitled. Section 32 of the Partnership Act provides for retirement of a partner from the partnership but it makes no provision of separation of share of the retired partner but this matter has been left to be determined by agreement between the partners. <em><span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">In the case of Ajudhia Pershad Ram Pershad Vs. Sham Sunder and others, AIR 1947 Lahore,13 Cornelius J. </span></em>elaborately discussed this provision of the law and held as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>“There would thus appear to be no doubt that the share of a partner in an existing partnership is essentially movable property, notwithstanding that a part of the partnership property may be immovable.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of <em><span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Addanki Narayanappa Vs. Bhaskara Krishnappa, AIR 1966 SC 1300, </span></em>Indian Supreme Court held that “the interest of the partners of Addadki family in the partnership assets was movable property and the document evidencing the relinquishment of that interest was not compulsorily registerable under section 17(1) of the Registration Act.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">In this case reliance may be placed on the case of <em><span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Lui Ying Ping vs. Leon Fang AI.(1984) 36 DLR (AD)273, </span>t</em>he Court held as under:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>“In the instant case, the respondent by the agreement Ext.2(a), with her partner retired from the partnership and relinquished all her interests including her share in the land and building at Motijheel on consideration of cash payment of Tk.20,000/-. This document was not required to be registered under the Registration Act. Consequently, her interest in the land and building stood transferred to the appellant who thereupon converted all his assets into a proprietorship and mutated his name accordingly in all relevant public documents.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of <em><span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">N. Khandervali Saheb (dead) by LRS and another vs. N. Gudu Sahib (dead) and others (2003) 3 SCC 229, </span></em>the question arose whether an award by which residue assets of a partnership firm are distributed amongst the partners on dissolution of the partnership firm requires registration under section 17 of the Registration Act,1908. On dissolution of the partnership firm, accounts are settled amongst the partners and the assets of the partnership are distributed amongst the partners as per their respective shares in the </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: TimesNewRoman;">partnership firm. Thus, on dissolution of a partnership firm, the allotment of assets to individual partners is not a case of transfer of any assets of the firm. The assets which hereinbefore belonged to each partner will after dissolution of the firm stand allotted to the partners individually. There is no transfer or assignment of ownership in any of the assets. This is the legal consequence of distribution of assets on dissolution of a partnership firm. The distribution of assets may be done either by way of an arbitration award or by mutual settlement between the partners themselves. The document which records the settlement in this case is an award which does not require registration under section 17 of the Registration Act since the document does not transfer or assign interest in any asset.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case of </span><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'TimesNewRoman\,BoldItalic';">S.V. Chandra Pandian vs. S. V. Sivalinga Nadar (1993) 1 SCC 589, </span></em></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the Indian Supreme Court held that “the property falling to the share of the partner on distribution of the residue would naturally belong to him exclusively but since in the eye of law it is money and not immovable property there is no question of registration under section 17 of the Registration Act.” </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the above case, the Indian Supreme Court further held that if one looks at the award as allocating certain immovable property since there is no transfer, no partition or extinguishment of any right therein, there is no question of application of section 17(1) of the Registration Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This Division also relied upon the case of </span><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'TimesNewRoman\,BoldItalic';">Commissioner of Income Tax, West Bengal, Calcutta Vs. Juggilal Kamalapat, AIR 1967 (SC)401. </span></em></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The question arose whether non-registration of the relinquishment deed invalidates the transfer of the business assets to the new partnership.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'TimesNewRoman\,Bold';">The Supreme Court of India in the above case held as under:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>“The Deed of Relinquishment, in this case, was in respect of the individual interest of the three Singhania Brothers in the assets of the partnership firm in favour of the Kamla Town Trust, and consequently, did not require registration, even though the assets of the partnership firm included immovable property, and was valid without registration. As a result of this deed, all the assets of the partnership vested in the new partners of the firm.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Having considered the cases cited above, we find that a deed of dissolution of partnership is not required to be registered under section 17 of the Registration Act because the share of a partner in a partnership is essentially moveable property notwithstanding that a part of the partnership property may be immovable. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'TimesNewRoman\,Bold'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">The learned Counsel for the petitioners could not make out any case as contemplated under Order XLVII Rule 1 of the Code of Civil Procedure and as such, we do not find any ground for interference. Accordingly, this civil review petition is dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue_October__18(2)/Issue__OCTOBER_%2018(2)__C.%20Review%20315%20of%2017__Syed%20Mahmud%20Hossain,%20J__AD__4.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">CIVIL REVIEW PETITION No.315 OF 2017.</span></u></strong></a><u></u></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(From the judgment and order dated 24.05.2016 passed by this Division in Civil Appeal No.01 of 2010)</span></p></div></div></div></div>
679	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Bene Maritime Inc. Vs. Aman Feed Ltd. and others, (Muhammad Imman Ali, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL PETITION FOR  LEAVE TO APPEAL  No. 1003 OF 2018  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Syed Mahmud Hossain, CJ,  Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Hasan Foez Siddique, J Mirza Hussain Haider, J.  </p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Kamal-ul-Alam, senior Advocate, instructed by  Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)     </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2018</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Bene Maritime Inc.  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Aman Feed Limited and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Admiralty Court Act  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">(CIVIL</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin-left: 0in; text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue_October__18(2)/Issue__OCTOBER_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%201003%20of%2018__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali__AD__1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Bene Maritime Inc. </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Petitioner </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Aman Feed Limited and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondents</span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt;">Admiralty Court Act (XLIII of 2000)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 3</span> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">We are of the view that ends of justice would </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">be</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> sufficiently met if the plaintiff, respondent</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">No.1 </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.1pt;">herein, is directed to furnish appropriate</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.1pt;"> General</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> Average Bond and General Average Guarantee in the sum of US$ 180,000.00 as assessed by Albatross Adjusters Limited (annexed in the additional paper book dated 26.02.2018). On furnishing the aforesaid General Average Bond and General Average Guarantee in favour of the ship owners, the petitioner herein, shall discharge the cargo as directed by the Admiralty Court</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                   </span>...(9 and 10)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; letter-spacing: -.3pt; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For the Petitioner:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr. Kamal-ul-Alam,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;"> senior Advocate, instructed by <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; background: white; mso-highlight: white; mso-ansi-language: EN;">For Respondent:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Mr Rokunuddin Mahmud, Senior <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Advocate with Mr. M. Hafizullah, Senior Advocate and Mr. Oliullah, Advocate instructed by <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Mr. Zainul Abedin, <span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 112%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><h4 style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; text-align: justify;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-variant: small-caps; mso-font-width: 110%;">Muhammad Imman Ali, J</span></u><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">:</span></u> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-weight: normal; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">This civil Petition for leave to appeal is directred against the order dated 12<sup>th</sup> day of February, 2018 passed by the Admiralty Bench of the High Court Division in Admiralty Suit No.5 of 2018 allowing the application filed by the plaintiff to deliver the cargo of 28,200.57 MTs of Soyabean Meal/Extraction.</span></h4><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts, relevant for disposal of this civil petition for leave to appeal, are that respondent No.1, Aman Feed Limited imported 28,200.57 MTs Soyabean Meal/Extraction which arrived at Chittagong Port on board vessel M.V. BENE. Respondent No.1 as the plaintiff filed Admiralty Suit No.5 of 2018 before the Admiralty Bench of the High Court Division praying for a decree in the sum of taka <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">18,51,29,195.79 equivalent to US$ 22,17,116.11.</span> In that admiralty suit, the plaintiff filed and application for direction upon defendant Nos.1-4 for immediate delivery of 28,200.570 MTs of Soyabean Meal/Extraction from vessel M.V. BENE which was lying at Chittagong Port.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Defendant No.3, owner of Vessel M.V. BENE (the petitioner herein) appeared in the suit and filed written objection against the application for direction upon the plaintiff to furnish General Average Bond and General Average Guarantee before obtaining the delivery of the cargo. In the meantime, the plaintiff had obtained and order of arrest of defendant No.1 vessel on 25.01.2018.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By the impugned order dated 12.02.2018, the Admiralty Court allowed the application praying for direction for delivery of the cargo and at the same time rejected the prayer of the petitioner for direction upon the plaintiff to furnish General Average Bord and General Average Guarantee.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We heard Mr. Kamal-ul-Alam, learned Senior Advocate, appearing for the petitioner and Mr. Rokunuddin Mahmud, learned Senior Advocate with Mr. M. Hafizullah, learned Senior Advocate and Mr. Oliullah, learned Advocate, appearing for the respondents.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We find from the impugned order that the Admiralty Court noted that the question of declaration of General Average Bond and signing of General Average Guarantee by the plaintiff is out of ambit of the jurisdiction of this Court (the Admiralty Bench of the High Court Division and falls under the purview of arbitration and that this Court lacks jurisdiction to enter into the issue, since the same squarely falls within the jurisdiction of the Arbitral Tribunal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have considered the submissions made by the learned Counsel appearing for the parties concerned.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The matter of entitlement to General Average Bond and sea-worthiness of the vessel </span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">will undoubtedly be decided by the Arbitral Tribunal. We are of the view that before delivery of the cargo, the interest of the vessel is required to be protected by way of some security.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in .25in 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">9.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">In the facts and circumstances, we are of the view that ends of justice would be sufficiently met if the plaintiff, respondent No.1 herein, is directed to furnish appropriate General Average Bond and General Average Guarantee in the sum of US$ 180,000.00 as assessed by Albatross Adjusters Limited (annexed in the additional paper book dated 26.02.2018).</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in .25in 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">10.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">On furnishing the aforesaid General Average Bond and General Average Guarantee in favour of the ship owners, the petitioner herein, shall discharge the cargo as directed by the Admiralty Court. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in .25in 0in;"><span style="color: #000000;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -0.3pt;">11.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">With the above observations and directions, the civil petition for leave to appeal<span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> is disposed of.</span></span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></span></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue_October__18(2)/Issue__OCTOBER_%2018(2)__C.%20P.%201003%20of%2018__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali__AD__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">CIVIL PETITION</span></u></strong></a><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> FOR<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>LEAVE TO APPEAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>No. 1003 OF 2018.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgment and order dated 12<sup>th</sup> of February, 2018 passed by the High Court Division in Admiralty Suit No.5 of 2018).</span></p></div></div></div></div>
680	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Chairman, DC, Feni  Vs. Feni Alia Madrasha Committee, (Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J.) </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APPEAL No. 36 OF 2011  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J Nazmun Ara Sultana, J Muhammad Imman Ali, J, Md. Nawab Ali (dead), Advocate-on-Record,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ (AD)     </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2016</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  The Chairman, District Council, Feni, Deputy Commissioner, Feni </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Feni alia Madrasha Mosque Committee </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Local Government Ordinance  </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; text-align: right; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Appellant </span></strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-Versus</span></strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">-</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%; color: #000000;">Feni alia Madrasha Mosque Committee</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">. . . Respondent</span></strong></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; text-align: left;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11pt;">Local Government Ordinance</span></strong><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> (52 of 1976)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: left;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 91</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Although there is no consequence in the section the very language that no suit shall be instituted against a local parishad ... until the expiration of one month after notice in writing has been delivered or left at its office and that the plaint shall contain a statement that such notice has been so delivered or left </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">clearly shows that service of notice as required</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">by section 91 of the Ordinance was mandatory</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> and in the absence of such notice, the suit could not be instituted, in other words the suit could not be maintained.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>. . .(11)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Local Government Ordinance, (52 of 1976)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Sections 91 and 92</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Single Bench of the High Court Division considering the provisions of sections 91 and 92 of the Pourashava Ordinance held that where there are mandatory provision of law to be complied with before filing a suit, such provision must be complied with before institution of the suit. In the case in hand since the provision of section 91 of the Ordinance was not complied with the suit was not maintainable. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Service of notice under section 91 of the Ordinance upon the District Council, Feni (at the time of filing the suit, it was Noakhali) was a must before institution of the suit and as admittedly no notice as required by the said section of the Ordinance was delivered or left at the office of the District Council, Noakhali (now Feni) before the institution of the suit, the suit was not maintainable in law and the same </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">was liable to be dismissed on the ground of its</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> maintainability alone without deciding the other issues involved in the suit. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>. . . (15 and 16)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.5pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Trustees of the Port of Chittagong Vs. Sadharon</span></em></strong><strong><em><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Bima Corporation and others, 32 DLR 99; Nur Muhammad and others Vs. Moulvi Mainuddin Ahmed and others, 39 DLR (AD) 1; Narayongonj Poueashava, 46 DLR 295; Abul Bashar Sowdagar and others Vs. Bacha Mea and others 59 DLR (2007) 112 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">For the Appellants:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> Syed Amirul Islam,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> Senior Advocate instructed by Mr. Md. Nawab Ali (dead), Advocate-on-Record</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">For the Respondent:</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> <em>Ex-pate</em></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 112%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">Md. Abdul Wahhab Miah, J</span></u></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps;">:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">This appeal, by leave, is from the judgment and order dated the 20th day of August, 2009 passed by a Single Judge of the High Court Division in Civil Revision No.2785 of 2004 making the Rule absolute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: list 0in left 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Facts necessary to dispose this appeal are that respondent No.1 as the plaintiff instituted Title Suit No.138 of 1981 in the Court of the then Munsif (now Assistant Judge), 2nd Court, Feni Sadar, Feni for the following principal relief:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ó(K) wb¤œ ZcwQj ewY©Z cyKzi eveZ 1bs weev`x nB‡Z 4bs weev`x 2/3 bs weev`xi †hvMv‡hv‡M 10/08/81 Bs Zvwi‡L nvwmjK…Z bvwjkx e‡›`ve¯Í m¤ú~Y© ZÂK, †hvM‡hvM, †e-ABbx, f~qv, ÿgZvi ewnf~Z©, AKvh©Kvix Ges ev`xi Dci eva¨Ki n‡b g‡g© ev`x‡K weev`xMY weiæ‡× wWwµ `v‡bi,</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> envj _vKve¯’vq Ges ev`x gmwR‡`i ¯^Z¡ `Lj envj _vKvKvjxb 1-3 bs weev`x †hb Kvnv‡KI bvwjkx cyKzi e‡›`ve¯Í<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>bv †`q Ges 1-4 bs weev`x †hb bvwjkx cyKz‡i cÖ‡ek bv K‡i I bvwjkx cyKzi e‡›`ve¯Í bv †`q Ges 1-4 bs weev`x †hb bvwjkx cyKz‡i cÖ‡ek bv K‡i| ev`x‡K bvwjkx cyKzi nB‡Z †e`Lj bv K‡i Zrg‡g© 1-4 bs weev`xi weiæ‡× ¯’vqx wb‡lavÁvi wWwµ`v‡bi Ges bvwjkx cyKzi ewa©Z ev`x gmwR` </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Wakf By Immemorial user</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ;
